    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5764566441833913018">(BACK COVER)<br/><br/>Why does Ted Bernal Guevara keep putting out these James Dean conceptual novels? In plain truth, Guevara says, “He’s like a kid (James Dean) I went to class with, rode the bus with and slid down an awesome snow-packed hill with.” And after high school, he goes on to Hollywood fame and immortality while Guevara from his modest bookish world is left to wonder abo</span>
  <span id="freeText5764566441833913018" style="display:none">(BACK COVER)<br /><br />Why does Ted Bernal Guevara keep putting out these James Dean conceptual novels? In plain truth, Guevara says, “He’s like a kid (James Dean) I went to class with, rode the bus with and slid down an awesome snow-packed hill with.” And after high school, he goes on to Hollywood fame and immortality while Guevara from his modest bookish world is left to wonder about the iconic image, giving it a stark, poignant voice sixty years later. Guevara grew up in Marion, Indiana, where the actor was born. <br /><br />In 1954, Dean met perhaps the one real romance of his brief life. Italian actress Pier Angeli was barely 22 when her movie The Silver Chalice coincided with Dean’s East of Eden at Warner Brothers. She’d sneak over to watch him perform, and he would do the same. When they finally interact, Pier’s mother disapproves of Dean’s behavior, attire and not being Catholic.<br /><br />Some say it was all for the limelight and publicity. Guevara’s gripping and frank story vies otherwise, excavating the actor’s true passion for the lovely but quaint Ms. Angeli.<br /><br />Guevara is also the author of True Feel, A Circle with Two Corners, and Days of Slint, the first James Dean conceptual novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5764566441833913018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1440433760?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deon" href="/user/show/25136988-deon">Deon</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1440433760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12301768801411112025">This book irked me a little. Everyone wants to manipulate the corpse of James Dean. Not me, and admitting that is wanting everything to stay the same. Hey, we're all fanatics here. Reading it I saw a lot of myself in Dean, in a normal crazy sense. Am I going to buy an unprotected Porsche and drive it a hundred miles per hour? I hope not. But the author does great on injecting normalcy, or rather on the calming of the actor’s hectic disposition leading an abnormal life. What isn’t in Hollywood? M</span>
  <span id="freeText12301768801411112025" style="display:none">This book irked me a little. Everyone wants to manipulate the corpse of James Dean. Not me, and admitting that is wanting everything to stay the same. Hey, we're all fanatics here. Reading it I saw a lot of myself in Dean, in a normal crazy sense. Am I going to buy an unprotected Porsche and drive it a hundred miles per hour? I hope not. But the author does great on injecting normalcy, or rather on the calming of the actor’s hectic disposition leading an abnormal life. What isn’t in Hollywood? Maybe Dean's just a regular guy who can fall in love and not get out of it so easy, like any of us. At any rate Ted Bernal Guevara did his research and made his story, his profile of Dean, look like fun fiction. But the truth in it I ate like pumpkin pie.</span>

<div id="review_1428778171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428778171" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48409828-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447320691p2/48409828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1428778171?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/48409828-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428778171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2215513317447497352">Recently, Ted Bernal Guevara posted in his Facebook “[James Dean] loved to laugh, always made use of the moment as lively as possible, or else…” This maybe. But the author seemed to forget the waning in his novel, Lips of a Mastodon. Though, the writing is good, and the plot seems to be in order, his profile of the actor is soaked in booze and “experimental” drug use. Happiness in the moment does not exist. Whether the escape is from the denial of Pier Angeli or from a rough youth, the actor her</span>
  <span id="freeText2215513317447497352" style="display:none">Recently, Ted Bernal Guevara posted in his Facebook “[James Dean] loved to laugh, always made use of the moment as lively as possible, or else…” This maybe. But the author seemed to forget the waning in his novel, Lips of a Mastodon. Though, the writing is good, and the plot seems to be in order, his profile of the actor is soaked in booze and “experimental” drug use. Happiness in the moment does not exist. Whether the escape is from the denial of Pier Angeli or from a rough youth, the actor here is certainly not a happy camper.<br /><br />But there is light fun in the courtship itself. Guevara went as far as placing the couple in a funny near wife-swapping incident, which could only hint at that James Dean had every intention to marry Pier Angeli. The book reads quickly—no clear-cut chapters—just like the affair that occurred during the making of their two Warner Bros. films, side by side. <br /><br />Guevara doesn’t retract so much on the actor’s other vague yarns. If he does, on sporadic occasions, the points made are, well, vague. He does linger on the character, Will Carp, who is full of envy of the actor that it hides Carp's true sexual nature toward Dean. It's the 1950s. Closets are full. To Dean, image was everything.<br /><br />But Guevara concentrates on the love story, its happy times and pitfalls, and does it effectively. This book might just be for romantics who love to pain themselves in moments and laugh on other. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2215513317447497352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1455442613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455442613" />
    <a title="Elis David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23296676-elis-david"><img alt="Elis David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377123786p2/23296676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455442613?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elis David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elis David" href="/user/show/23296676-elis-david">Elis David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455442613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9289761994886299005">I found this novel to be informative and entertaining, a sympathetic depiction of James Dean, the Indiana-born actor who made three major films in less than two years. Most of what was written in the book had a fresh take. Dean’s affair with Pier Angeli, with all the vibrant, offbeat, sometime hilarious details, was new to me so it held my interest. But it was a sad story of a guy trying to fit a new girl in his life, to somehow replace the tragedy of his mother’s death while he was under the ro</span>
  <span id="freeText9289761994886299005" style="display:none">I found this novel to be informative and entertaining, a sympathetic depiction of James Dean, the Indiana-born actor who made three major films in less than two years. Most of what was written in the book had a fresh take. Dean’s affair with Pier Angeli, with all the vibrant, offbeat, sometime hilarious details, was new to me so it held my interest. But it was a sad story of a guy trying to fit a new girl in his life, to somehow replace the tragedy of his mother’s death while he was under the roof his domineering father and a neutral step mother. Although things are settling in, Dean still recalls the abandonment of his father putting him in a train to go back to Indiana alone. <br /><br />Pier Angeli, a splash-in-the-pan star compared to Dean, seemed torn between her family and Dean and had no backbone whatsoever on whom to choose. However, she is happiest when she is with Dean. Her movie Silver Chalice was also a bygone compared to Dean’s East of Eden. So, there was an obvious clinging to greatness in Pier.<br /><br />The author makes the love affair appealing, provocative and needed, in both of the characters’ fates, and all the subplots and going-ons worked as well. Overall, it is new approach, one that keeps you reading and entertained.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9289761994886299005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer845167757576713935">The concept is simple: extend East of Eden. I saw the movie some 20 years ago, and this novel, Lips of a Mastodon, made me want to analyze that movie some more. So I watched it again. And sure enough, evidence of balance between evolution and creationism are in both stories. Guevara uses the actor Ray Massey to further the idea, revealing an aftermath friendship with James Dean, basing it on who's-to-know. Not all the days of the rebel actor were recorded.   <span id="freeText845167757576713935" style="display:none">The concept is simple: extend East of Eden. I saw the movie some 20 years ago, and this novel, Lips of a Mastodon, made me want to analyze that movie some more. So I watched it again. And sure enough, evidence of balance between evolution and creationism are in both stories. Guevara uses the actor Ray Massey to further the idea, revealing an aftermath friendship with James Dean, basing it on who's-to-know. Not all the days of the rebel actor were recorded. This could have happened. <br /><br />This subplot nicely compliments the love affair with Pier Angeli and all that is burdening the actor during his short life.<br /><br />More brooding on this may well make me tackle John Steinbeck's East of Eden, the real McCoy. Lips of a Mastodon can cause such an addiction. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17944971897052224294">This may be. But try reading this book aloud and you can almost hear a young man telling a more spruced-up gut story than the one from the dust. This was such a hard candy read for me that I am loss for words. But here try I: <br/><br/>The narrator (obviously James Dean) is vocal rather than typing on a page, just a notch below a guy with a recorder and a mike. The story first follows a day-to-day happening after Dean meets the seemingly plain Pier Angeli, then it goes all over the place after he meets th</span>
  <span id="freeText17944971897052224294" style="display:none">This may be. But try reading this book aloud and you can almost hear a young man telling a more spruced-up gut story than the one from the dust. This was such a hard candy read for me that I am loss for words. But here try I: <br /><br />The narrator (obviously James Dean) is vocal rather than typing on a page, just a notch below a guy with a recorder and a mike. The story first follows a day-to-day happening after Dean meets the seemingly plain Pier Angeli, then it goes all over the place after he meets the wrestler-like figure of Pier’s mother. In most nonfiction books, she’s just a pancake-flat footnote, but here she’s the villain in the trench coat. It takes a while for her and Dean to rumble in the course of the affair, all because he is down-home touchy-feely to everybody.<br /> <br />I read through it easy enough. It's about a guy flipping a finger at tradition because it is at his blindside. When it catches up with him, he tries to dismantle it according to his habits and needs. Big problem.<br /><br />The story has a Romeo and Juliet bent to it, but Romeo here just wants comfortable, no-hassle sex from Juliet. And in it, his longing for her real self develops. This has language, sex, a bit of drive-thru drugs and cameos from Marlon Brando and such.<br /><br />A totally mild yet crazy, in your face, fun read. Yeah, I recommend it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17944971897052224294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1463936794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1463936794" />
    <a title="Crazy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49860582-crazy"><img alt="Crazy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449636092p2/49860582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1463936794?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crazy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crazy" href="/user/show/49860582-crazy">Crazy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1463936794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14283014783740006782">This book is far more solid and upbeat(!) than I had expected it to be, and can be enjoyed at many levels from plot to its nostalgic aspect. I'm used to highly intellectual fiction, which this has some and I thoroughly enjoyed. Yet despite its exploration of the life of a tragic figure (James Dean is such), it manages to be light-hearted. <br/><br/>It's satirical as well; so much so that it bogs down any reference to any sad outcome. If anything it more closely resembles the mysticism of one J.D. Salinger</span>
  <span id="freeText14283014783740006782" style="display:none">This book is far more solid and upbeat(!) than I had expected it to be, and can be enjoyed at many levels from plot to its nostalgic aspect. I'm used to highly intellectual fiction, which this has some and I thoroughly enjoyed. Yet despite its exploration of the life of a tragic figure (James Dean is such), it manages to be light-hearted. <br /><br />It's satirical as well; so much so that it bogs down any reference to any sad outcome. If anything it more closely resembles the mysticism of one J.D. Salinger—if I don’t reach too high of a comparison. The first-person voice of a come-what-may figure on his first major break as an artist could have come off as pretentious and annoying, but instead it is calming and humorous. <br /><br />That said, while I would recommend it to people seeking many different reading experiences, I can give this 5 stars because it sets out what it aims for. It doesn’t pretend to leap bounds over complexities, as in Catcher in the Rye, maybe Guevara’s bowing stance to the mighty Salinger (there I go again). Still, it will be worth rereading once it passes, as always, the test of time. <br /><br />Did I just say that? First, it has to get over the small-press hump. Rumble Lit?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14283014783740006782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1470217153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470217153" />
    <a title="David Sullivan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50160944-david-sullivan"><img alt="David Sullivan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450266312p2/50160944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470217153?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sullivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sullivan" href="/user/show/50160944-david-sullivan">David Sullivan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470217153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17851022933820187844">I read True Feel last year and loved it so much that I wanted to experience more of this still quite unknown author.<br/><br/>Lips of a Mastodon was a complete u-turn in style and approach. I'm not sure if it’s biography gone fiction, considering in the back of the book, Guevara admits [James Dean] is "like a kid I went to class with…" which suggests to me a bond closer than fanfare or even from a biographer looking in too deep. The best way I know to describe this novel is: a mix of Chuck Palahniuk and F</span>
  <span id="freeText17851022933820187844" style="display:none">I read True Feel last year and loved it so much that I wanted to experience more of this still quite unknown author.<br /><br />Lips of a Mastodon was a complete u-turn in style and approach. I'm not sure if it’s biography gone fiction, considering in the back of the book, Guevara admits [James Dean] is "like a kid I went to class with…" which suggests to me a bond closer than fanfare or even from a biographer looking in too deep. The best way I know to describe this novel is: a mix of Chuck Palahniuk and Fifty Shades of Grey. (Don't panic, people - I haven't read and don't intend to read Fifty Shades. I've heard enough about it to use it as a comparison.)<br /><br />I love the way Guevara puts words together. I love the way he ties poetic lines and make them narrative. I love the way he develops characters; their backgrounds sink deep and find fresh drinkable water.<br /><br />But this one is a different angle with the same texture. Less sub characters in this one, and that romance bit, it doesn’t quite ruin my appetite here. Which is to say... there's no way I could have completely embraced this book as a whole.<br /><br />I recommend Lips of a Mastodon to you. But if you want to read a more fantastic book by this author, read his collage of characters, which is True Feel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17851022933820187844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13146226946324974730" style="display:none">We, my husband and I, agree with most of what is claimed under this novel, just not quite sure of how high the star rating gets! True, this unknown author has potential, perhaps a smooth quality to his writing, so fluid one tends to overlook grammatical errors. I found six. But yes, over time they can just be part of the book's characteristic. <br /><br />The plot is in order enough, day to day. One thing I see is every time that there's crisis, the flow of the narrative also goes asunder, not just in the actions of the "I" person. I can call him the narrator, but he seems not to want that role. <br /><br />The rest of the characters are well-rounded, but nothing out of the ordinary. Some are close to being alike. <br /><br />This book is fiction, but the author is scraping his knees over actual past. He chooses that over pushing Hollywood nostalgia, which is perhaps the main attraction this book has to bait us into picking up a copy.<br /><br />If there is a three and a half stars I could click, it would be that. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14480890542592442473">From the cover of this book, I can see the attraction constantly building up to the actor James Dean. He was a good looking person! And since he passed a good sixty years ago, the following to his legacy has become complex due to his looks. Stories have developed left and right, I imagine, and fans tend to pick the ones they're comfortable with, the way they want their idol to be.<br/><br/>With that in mind, Lips of a Mastodon is careful not to spoil anyone's joyous celebration. It claims itself fiction. </span>
  <span id="freeText14480890542592442473" style="display:none">From the cover of this book, I can see the attraction constantly building up to the actor James Dean. He was a good looking person! And since he passed a good sixty years ago, the following to his legacy has become complex due to his looks. Stories have developed left and right, I imagine, and fans tend to pick the ones they're comfortable with, the way they want their idol to be.<br /><br />With that in mind, Lips of a Mastodon is careful not to spoil anyone's joyous celebration. It claims itself fiction. But the based-on events are true, the affair with Pier Angeli, the making of East of Eden and Dean's interactions with both famed stars and every day people he associated himself with.<br /><br />All the author had to do was piece the events together, with incredible transitions, to incorporate this remarkable, funny, emotionally draining story. I am not yet caught up in the fanaticism...but I did enjoy this novel. <br /> </span>

  <span id="freeText1141053666180629694" style="display:none">Lips of a Mastodon is the story of James Dean's brief stint with the Italian actress Pier Angeli. In fact the author or a disclaimer jots it down in the opening pages: This is a work of fiction.<br /><br />But with the cover, one of the more famous photos of the couple, the book says I have this "in cement, enjoy it, for it had taken place...."<br /><br />The "this" is a love story as it had never been told before, a little dirt, a little grungy, a little cinematic. <span id="freeTextContainer7201146507667919864">One thing that lacks in the front cover or what this novel recommends before reading it is the note: YOU MUST BE A JAMES DEAN FAN!   <span id="freeText7201146507667919864" style="display:none">One thing that lacks in the front cover or what this novel recommends before reading it is the note: YOU MUST BE A JAMES DEAN FAN! Guevara ventures on putting out a story written for the general adult audience and gambles on "You don't need to know my characters beforehand. Just enjoy my narrative."<br /><br />Bold aim. <div id="review_1724139524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1724139524" />
    <a title="Neil Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58509506-neil-jones"><img alt="Neil Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470807648p2/58509506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1724139524?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil Jones" href="/user/show/58509506-neil-jones">Neil Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1724139524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14519321633666813456">I was gifted this book by the author. We struck up a casual conversation one day and to my surprise he said, "I like to write." I thought, "Okay? That's nice." But as we kept talking I knew he was serious. Mr. Guevara convinced me not by asking me to read, but by his passion for it. We talked about The Great Gatsby and other books we've both read. He vowed to bring me a copy of his latest book, "Lips of a Mastodon." And low and behold the next day he brought it in for me, signed and all. So I re</span>
  <span id="freeText14519321633666813456" style="display:none">I was gifted this book by the author. We struck up a casual conversation one day and to my surprise he said, "I like to write." I thought, "Okay? That's nice." But as we kept talking I knew he was serious. Mr. Guevara convinced me not by asking me to read, but by his passion for it. We talked about The Great Gatsby and other books we've both read. He vowed to bring me a copy of his latest book, "Lips of a Mastodon." And low and behold the next day he brought it in for me, signed and all. So I read it. And by God it was one of the best books I have read. Ted is a masterful artist with his words. Sometimes I had to go back and reread some paragraphs because I was so delighted with the wordplay. I am a Southern man by heart and have lived in his home state of Indiana for well over 2 years. And this book strikes home. I didn't know much about James Dean before reading this novel. But now I am sad to say that after going for a right in that bright red MG-TD of his. Speeding up and down the highways at light-speed. This book will give you whiplash, in a good way. You're almost there with Jimmie, pulling for him, fighting beside him, loving the character that has been portrayed. I rated this book 5 out of 5 and solemnly stand by that rating. Not because Ted is my friend, but because this is a damn good book. Grab a copy and you'll know what I mean. <br /><br />- Neil</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1461338436" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1461338436?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malco" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malco" href="/user/show/49754312-malco">Malco</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461338436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13465665549111403509">I dig the fact that Mr. Guevara tries to inject the icon actor James Dean as a homespun, properly brought up young man before he came to Hollywood. But in truth Dean came from New York City before the filming of East of Eden, the time this novel is situated in, and had done all the damage to his reputation, in NYC.<br/><br/>From this, I can tell you Guevara is a James Dean diehard fan, a “Deaner” they call it in Indiana. He is constantly repairing the image, the vulgar attitude, the high and mighty confid</span>
  <span id="freeText13465665549111403509" style="display:none">I dig the fact that Mr. Guevara tries to inject the icon actor James Dean as a homespun, properly brought up young man before he came to Hollywood. But in truth Dean came from New York City before the filming of East of Eden, the time this novel is situated in, and had done all the damage to his reputation, in NYC.<br /><br />From this, I can tell you Guevara is a James Dean diehard fan, a “Deaner” they call it in Indiana. He is constantly repairing the image, the vulgar attitude, the high and mighty confidence, and lastly the sleep-with-anyone-who-would-give-me-a-break venue.<br /><br />With the actor’s fling with Pier Angeli, all these characteristics diminish into good and wholesome. Lips of a Mastodon takes it one step higher with the image. It puts it in a celestial, do-good, above evil realm. But once you get my meaning, keep on reading. It does have all the properties of being a novel, the only way Guevara can put his arms around all the fat.<br /><br />I read it and examined it because my cousin left it in my apartment. He and I, too, are Deaners, just outside of Indiana.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13465665549111403509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1462337557?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda M" href="/user/show/39095220-melinda-m">Melinda M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39095220-melinda-m?shelf=first-reads-done">first-reads-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39095220-melinda-m?shelf=done">done</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1462337557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4623756037978840021">Lips Of a Mastodon is fiction but gives a voice to James Dean's love affair with Italian actress Pier Angeli in 1954. It is well written. Ted Bernal Guevara makes you feel as if James Dean is telling the story. It is a fast read and an interesting story.<br/><br/>I received. this book thru Goodreads Giveaways</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1533806159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Syno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Syno" href="/user/show/52203789-syno">Syno</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533806159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2848888623088204374">The characterization of James Dean in this novel uses death as a primary tool. He is narrating from the grave. Though at peace, he prefers life, to the exact moment of the love he once knew. Interesting. Worth my time at night, at a toll booth. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o7Lgs3f4xA9zW6ycjl3soKeMgq3shJdvnH9gN4xZTVSZlIlhzKYNZ9RwGP15qOZ/cdNlZSIJGQjHASaGQRq/zg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gX9qeXq5k9dEeDLKBMrNRHhCIHoPrr80ToTGjbPU1Mi7WQOrwedav+NThqvzP8ebrh3HssEjMVMV+oA8fpcmUg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4251995.Ted_Bernal_Guevara">About Ted Bernal Guevara</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4251995.Ted_Bernal_Guevara"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1369308180p3/4251995.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4251995.Ted_Bernal_Guevara">Ted Bernal Guevara
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
147
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8860978124599958426">Ted Bernal Guevara has an upcoming novel, How to Design a Threshold, in October, about a clairvoyant comic priest out to save New York City. <br/><br/>Mr. Guevara resides in South Carolina, where he is a freelance writer. He is the author of two James Dean conceptual novels, Days of Slint and Lips of a Mastodon. His first novel, A Circle with Two Corners, won praises from Midwest reviews, including one from</span>
  <span id="freeText8860978124599958426" style="display:none">Ted Bernal Guevara has an upcoming novel, How to Design a Threshold, in October, about a clairvoyant comic priest out to save New York City. <br /><br />Mr. Guevara resides in South Carolina, where he is a freelance writer. He is the author of two James Dean conceptual novels, Days of Slint and Lips of a Mastodon. His first novel, A Circle with Two Corners, won praises from Midwest reviews, including one from The Sentinel. The crime-romance novel, True Feel, is in its Second Edition.<br /><br />Ted has also published three volumes of poetry, Films, Birds on Elephant, and Tonto and Destinata.<br /><br />Although he delves in an array of themes, always looking for the unusual and the edgy, Guevara finds adherence in the plight of the disabled and all their "profound richness," as he states in a poem.<br /><br />At age 9, his family moved from the Philippines to Marion, Indiana—where all his physical challenges were realized and at same time, rewarded. His physician father never taught him how to dribble a basketball but had trained him to type a thousand words per day, from notable books, to increase his typing speed. Ted caught the literary bug instead from the exercise.<br /><br />Kirkus considers Mr. Guevara as Author to Watch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8860978124599958426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
